<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p3" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p3" class="link-target"></a><p>subject to the probabilistic constraints<a name="pcbi.1003665.e055" id="pcbi.1003665.e055" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e055" class="inline-graphic"></span><a name="pcbi.1003665.e056" id="pcbi.1003665.e056" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e056" class="inline-graphic"></span></p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p4" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p4" class="link-target"></a><p>Given the 1-of-<span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e057" class="inline-graphic"></span> representation of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e058" class="inline-graphic"></span>, this may be written as<a name="pcbi.1003665.e059" id="pcbi.1003665.e059" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e059" class="inline-graphic"><span class="note">(2)</span></span></p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p5" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p5" class="link-target"></a><p>Similarly, the conditional distribution <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e060" class="inline-graphic"></span> that a VAF <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e061" class="inline-graphic"></span> arises from the mixture may be written<a name="pcbi.1003665.e062" id="pcbi.1003665.e062" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e062" class="inline-graphic"><span class="note">(3)</span></span>in terms of the shape parameter vectors <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e063" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e064" class="inline-graphic"></span> of the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e065" class="inline-graphic"></span> beta component, with aggregate parameters <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e066" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e067" class="inline-graphic"></span>.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p6" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p6" class="link-target"></a><p>To accommodate binomial and Gaussian mixture models in addition to the beta mixture model, we introduce abstract notation used below to define quantities (e.g., <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e068" class="inline-graphic"></span>-values) independently of the concrete representation of likelihoods and posterior distributions. We begin by defining abstract parameters <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e069" class="inline-graphic"></span>, which differ according to the model, i.e., beta, binomial, or Gaussian. For example, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e070" class="inline-graphic"></span>, with <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e071" class="inline-graphic"></span>. Further, while the Gaussian mixture model is also a function of VAFs <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e072" class="inline-graphic"></span>, the binomial mixture model is defined with respect to the variant and reference count vectors, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e073" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e074" class="inline-graphic"></span>, respectively. To abstract away these details, we use the notation <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e075" class="inline-graphic"></span> to denote the VAFs <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e076" class="inline-graphic"></span> of a beta or Gaussian mixture model or the counts <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e077" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e078" class="inline-graphic"></span> of a binomial mixture model, when convenient. In particular, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e079" class="inline-graphic"></span>, while <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e080" class="inline-graphic"></span>, with <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e081" class="inline-graphic"></span>.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p7" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p7" class="link-target"></a><p><a href="#pcbi.1003665.e059">Eqns. (2</a>) and (3) extended across the entire set <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e082" class="inline-graphic"></span> of VAFs (or, more abstractly, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e083" class="inline-graphic"></span> of data) and their associated latent variables <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e084" class="inline-graphic"></span> are combined to express the complete-data (i.e., including the latent variables) likelihood<a name="pcbi.1003665.e085" id="pcbi.1003665.e085" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e085" class="inline-graphic"><span class="note">(4)</span></span>which may be summed over <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e086" class="inline-graphic"></span> to give the incomplete likelihood<a name="pcbi.1003665.e087" id="pcbi.1003665.e087" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e087" class="inline-graphic"></span></p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p8" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p8" class="link-target"></a><p>These equations could be used to fit the beta parameters using expectation maximization (EM) or Markov chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) techniques.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p9" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p9" class="link-target"></a><p>We instead use a previously described <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Ma2" class="ref-tip">[43]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Fan1" class="ref-tip">[44]</a> variational Bayesian approach <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Bishop1" class="ref-tip">[40]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Beal1" class="ref-tip">[42]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Svensn1" class="ref-tip">[54]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Attias1" class="ref-tip">[58]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Attias2" class="ref-tip">[59]</a> to modeling a mixture of beta distributions. The general variational Bayesian theory and its application to mixture modeling are described in depth in several excellent references <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Bishop1" class="ref-tip">[40]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Beal1" class="ref-tip">[42]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Svensn1" class="ref-tip">[54]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Attias1" class="ref-tip">[58]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Attias2" class="ref-tip">[59]</a>. To establish consistent notation, we provide an abridged, but self-contained, introduction to this general theory and to its application to Gaussian <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Bishop1" class="ref-tip">[40]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Svensn1" class="ref-tip">[54]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Attias1" class="ref-tip">[58]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Attias2" class="ref-tip">[59]</a> and binomial mixture models in <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s010">Text S1</a>. Here, we summarize its application to beta mixture models to provide sufficient context for its use in and extension for clonality analysis. For full details of this derivation, the reader is referred to the original references <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Ma2" class="ref-tip">[43]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Fan1" class="ref-tip">[44]</a>.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p10" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p10" class="link-target"></a><p>Variational Bayesian beta mixture modeling approximates the posterior distribution, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e088" class="inline-graphic"></span>, over the model parameters <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e089" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e090" class="inline-graphic"></span>, and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e091" class="inline-graphic"></span> and the latent variables <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e092" class="inline-graphic"></span> with a distribution <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e093" class="inline-graphic"></span>. The form of this approximate distribution is a consequence of choice of prior distribution, whose product with the likelihood [Eq. (4)] defines the posterior <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e094" class="inline-graphic"></span> according to Bayes' theorem, and of the mild and standard <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Bishop1" class="ref-tip">[40]</a> assumption that the latent variables <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e095" class="inline-graphic"></span> factorize from the model parameters, i.e., <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e096" class="inline-graphic"></span>. This further simplifies, without assumption, to <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e097" class="inline-graphic"></span>. Finally, the authors assume the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e098" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e099" class="inline-graphic"></span> variables are independent and factorize to ultimately give <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e100" class="inline-graphic"></span>.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p11" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p11" class="link-target"></a><p>Ma and Leijon used four synthetic one-dimensional data sets (<a href="#pcbi-1003665-g004">Fig. 4</a> of Ref. 43), including two with highly overlapping beta distributions, to demonstrate the high accuracy of this method despite its assumption that the parameters of the beta distribution are independent. Fan et al. <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Fan1" class="ref-tip">[44]</a> additionally analyzed six three-dimensional data sets and similarly found that accuracy was not adversely effected by this factorization approximation (Table I of Ref. 44). Our own extensive simulation results further support these findings. We generated data sets by sampling a mixture of beta distributions in one, two, or three dimensions and having between two and five clusters (100 data sets for each dimensionality/number of clusters pair). <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s005">Fig. S5</a> shows the concordance (i.e., fraction of correctly assigned items) between the clustered and known results for each simulated data set. The average concordance is <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e101" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e102" class="inline-graphic"></span>, and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e103" class="inline-graphic"></span> in one, two, and three dimensions, respectively. Performance increases with dimensionality as the clusters become increasingly separated. This sparsity may be quantified by the minimum cluster self-overlap (see below). Data sets having a relatively small minimum cluster self-overlap have a relatively large overlap <em>between</em> clusters, which leads to uncertainty and degrading performance.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p12" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p12" class="link-target"></a><p>The prior distributions are generally selected to be conjugate to the likelihood for analytic convenience (e.g., see the derivations of the variational Bayesian Gaussian and binomial mixture models in <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s010">Text S1</a>). While a conjugate prior to the beta likelihood is formally available, its use would lead to an analytically intractable integration <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Ma2" class="ref-tip">[43]</a>. Therefore, Ma and Leijon <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Ma2" class="ref-tip">[43]</a> instead propose use of the following prior distribution<a name="pcbi.1003665.e104" id="pcbi.1003665.e104" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e104" class="inline-graphic"><span class="note">(5)</span></span>where <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e105" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e106" class="inline-graphic"></span> are gamma distributions<a name="pcbi.1003665.e107" id="pcbi.1003665.e107" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e107" class="inline-graphic"></span>and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e108" class="inline-graphic"></span> is the Dirichlet distribution<a name="pcbi.1003665.e109" id="pcbi.1003665.e109" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e109" class="inline-graphic"></span>over proportions <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e110" class="inline-graphic"></span>, with the normalizing constant <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e111" class="inline-graphic"></span><a name="pcbi.1003665.e112" id="pcbi.1003665.e112" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e112" class="inline-graphic"></span>and<a name="pcbi.1003665.e113" id="pcbi.1003665.e113" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e113" class="inline-graphic"></span></p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p13" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec1.p13" class="link-target"></a><p>The parameters of the approximate posterior distribution are now determined by iteratively minimizing the Kullback-Leibler divergence, a measure of the difference, between it and the posterior distribution, following the general prescription of variational Bayesian inference (see <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s010">Text S1</a>). The authors make a non-linear approximation to an expectation value arising during the iterative procedure so that the resulting, approximate posterior distribution has the form of a gamma distribution, despite the fact that the above gamma prior distribution is not conjugate to the beta likelihood. Significantly, the authors show that this additional approximation can be used to minimize the original, desired Kullback-Leibler divergence between the posterior distribution and the approximate, non-gamma posterior distribution. This results in the approximate posterior distribution<a name="pcbi.1003665.e114" id="pcbi.1003665.e114" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e114" class="inline-graphic"><span class="note">(6)</span></span>where <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e115" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e116" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e117" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e118" class="inline-graphic"></span>, and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e119" class="inline-graphic"></span> are defined in Eqns. 47–51, respectively, of Ref. 43. These parameters are updated from the corresponding initial hyperparameter values <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e120" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e121" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e122" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e123" class="inline-graphic"></span>, and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e124" class="inline-graphic"></span> as in a traditional EM iterative algorithm. It will also be convenient to define the posterior density with respect to the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e125" class="inline-graphic"></span> component<a name="pcbi.1003665.e126" id="pcbi.1003665.e126" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e126" class="inline-graphic"><span class="note">(7)</span></span></p>
</div>

<div id="section2" class="section toc-section"><a id="s4b" name="s4b" class="link-target" title="Probabilistic and hard cluster assignments"></a>
<h3>Probabilistic and hard cluster assignments</h3>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec2.p1" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec2.p1" class="link-target"></a><p>Variational Bayesian mixture models provide probabilistic assignments of variant <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e127" class="inline-graphic"></span> (i.e., a VAF <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e128" class="inline-graphic"></span> for beta or Gaussian mixture models or variant counts <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e129" class="inline-graphic"></span> for a binomial mixture model) to cluster <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e130" class="inline-graphic"></span> according to the posterior probabilities <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e131" class="inline-graphic"></span>. The <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e132" class="inline-graphic"></span> act as “responsibilities” and satisfy <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e133" class="inline-graphic"></span> In the case of the beta mixture model, the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e134" class="inline-graphic"></span> are defined by Eqns. 31 and 32 of Ref. 43. A more general derivation is provided in <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s010">Text S1</a>, along with specific calculations for binomial and Gaussian mixture models.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec2.p2" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec2.p2" class="link-target"></a><p>For visualization purposes, for example, we occasionally transform these probabilistic assignments into hard assignments, which assign <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e135" class="inline-graphic"></span> to one and only one cluster <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e136" class="inline-graphic"></span> according to<a name="pcbi.1003665.e137" id="pcbi.1003665.e137" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e137" class="inline-graphic"></span></p>
</div>

<div id="section3" class="section toc-section"><a id="s4c" name="s4c" class="link-target" title="Posterior predictive density"></a>
<h3>Posterior predictive density</h3>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec3.p1" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec3.p1" class="link-target"></a><p>The posterior predictive density gives the probability of a new (i.e., unobserved) variant, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e138" class="inline-graphic"></span>, given the observed data <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e139" class="inline-graphic"></span><a name="pcbi.1003665.e140" id="pcbi.1003665.e140" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e140" class="inline-graphic"></span>and all possible assignments <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e141" class="inline-graphic"></span> of that variant to a cluster. Evaluating the sum over <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e142" class="inline-graphic"></span>, making use of Eq. (2), gives<a name="pcbi.1003665.e143" id="pcbi.1003665.e143" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e143" class="inline-graphic"></span></p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec3.p2" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec3.p2" class="link-target"></a><p>We next approximate the true posterior distribution, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e144" class="inline-graphic"></span>, with the variational approximation <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e145" class="inline-graphic"></span> to give<a name="pcbi.1003665.e146" id="pcbi.1003665.e146" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e146" class="inline-graphic"></span></p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec3.p3" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec3.p3" class="link-target"></a><p>Since for all mixture models considered in this manuscript <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e147" class="inline-graphic"></span>, with <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e148" class="inline-graphic"></span> and<a name="pcbi.1003665.e149" id="pcbi.1003665.e149" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e149" class="inline-graphic"></span>this evaluates to<a name="pcbi.1003665.e150" id="pcbi.1003665.e150" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e150" class="inline-graphic"><span class="note">(8)</span></span></p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec3.p4" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec3.p4" class="link-target"></a><p>Ma and Leijon <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Ma2" class="ref-tip">[43]</a> assumed that <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e151" class="inline-graphic"></span>, where <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e152" class="inline-graphic"></span> is the Dirac delta function and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e153" class="inline-graphic"></span> are the converged parameter values, i.e., that the posterior distribution has negligible probability when any of the parameters differ from their converged values. In this case,<a name="pcbi.1003665.e154" id="pcbi.1003665.e154" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e154" class="inline-graphic"></span>which may be efficiently evaluated. We instead use Eq. (8), which avoids any assumption on the approximate posterior distribution. In the case of binomial and Gaussian mixture models, Eq. (8) may be evaluated analytically. In the case of a beta mixture model, for which <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e155" class="inline-graphic"></span> is given by Eq. (1) and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e156" class="inline-graphic"></span> is given by Eq. (7), we instead resort to numerical integration, evaluating data sampled from Eq. (7) via Eq. (1).</p>
</div>

<div id="section4" class="section toc-section"><a id="s4d" name="s4d" class="link-target" title="Prior initialization"></a>
<h3>Prior initialization</h3>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec4.p1" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec4.p1" class="link-target"></a><p>We choose hyperparameters resulting in prior distributions sufficiently broad to ensure that the number of clusters and their posterior parameterization are determined primarily from the data rather than from prior assumptions. In particular, following Ma and Leijon <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Ma2" class="ref-tip">[43]</a>, we choose <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e157" class="inline-graphic"></span> for all <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e158" class="inline-graphic"></span>. We also choose <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e159" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e160" class="inline-graphic"></span> for all <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e161" class="inline-graphic"></span>. Given the latter choice, the gamma distributions <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e162" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e163" class="inline-graphic"></span> collapse to exponential distributions. The resulting variances of these distributions, e.g., <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e164" class="inline-graphic"></span>, are large given our choice of hyperparameters and hence provide a broad prior.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec4.p2" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec4.p2" class="link-target"></a><p>We initialize the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e165" class="inline-graphic"></span> according to the hard assignments computed by <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e166" class="inline-graphic"></span>-means (provided in the R stats package and using default parameters, except with <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e167" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e168" class="inline-graphic"></span>). We initialize the parameters <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e169" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e170" class="inline-graphic"></span>, and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e171" class="inline-graphic"></span> to their respective hyperparameter values <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e172" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e173" class="inline-graphic"></span>, and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e174" class="inline-graphic"></span>. Finally, we initialize the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e175" class="inline-graphic"></span> such that the expected means of the cluster centers, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e176" class="inline-graphic"></span>, with <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e177" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e178" class="inline-graphic"></span>, are set to the values returned by <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e179" class="inline-graphic"></span>-means. We then perform the variational E step (i.e., calculate the expectations immediately following Eq. 51 of Ref. 43) <em>without</em> updating the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e180" class="inline-graphic"></span>, followed by the variational M step to update the parameters <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e181" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e182" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e183" class="inline-graphic"></span>, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e184" class="inline-graphic"></span>, and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e185" class="inline-graphic"></span> (via Eqns. 47–51 of Ref. 43). For the AML28 data set, this initialization results in the clusters shown in <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s006">Fig. S6a</a>. Initialization is followed by iteratively applying the variational E step (including updating the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e186" class="inline-graphic"></span>) and M step. To avoid undefined behavior in evaluating the beta distribution, we shift VAFs at zero or one by <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e187" class="inline-graphic"></span> or <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e188" class="inline-graphic"></span>, respectively, with <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e189" class="inline-graphic"></span> equal to machine precision.</p>
</div>

<div id="section5" class="section toc-section"><a id="s4e" name="s4e" class="link-target" title="Cluster pruning and outlier detection"></a>
<h3>Cluster pruning and outlier detection</h3>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p1" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p1" class="link-target"></a><p>Variational Bayesian mixture modeling generally discards clusters that do not contribute to the model, as determined by the data and strength of the prior distribution. Specifically, following convergence of the variational iteration and hard assignments of variants to clusters, we remove any clusters having less than the larger of three variants or 0.5% of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e190" class="inline-graphic"></span>, the total number of variants, assigned to them, a condition similar to our earlier approach <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Walter1" class="ref-tip">[14]</a>. If clusters are removed, the algorithm is again executed until convergence. For the beta mixture model, convergence is achieved when the absolute difference between all <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e191" class="inline-graphic"></span> across consecutive iterations is less than <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e192" class="inline-graphic"></span>. This condition differs slightly for binomial and Gaussian mixture models (see <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s010">Text S1</a>). The minimum cluster membership is motivated by the requirement of needing at least two proportions to fix the two degrees of freedom, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e193" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e194" class="inline-graphic"></span>, of a beta distribution. More intuitively, clustering is effectively a separation of intra- and inter-cluster distances. Defining an intra-cluster distance requires at least two items be assigned to that cluster.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p2" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p2" class="link-target"></a><p>To be conservative in our assessment of subclonality, we require clusters be well separated. Previously <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Walter1" class="ref-tip">[14]</a>, we used a condition on overlapping cluster standard error of the means to detect and remove overlapping clusters. Here, we instead adopt a quantitative notion of cluster overlap <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Korenblum1" class="ref-tip">[45]</a>, <a href="#pcbi.1003665-White1" class="ref-tip">[46]</a>, in which overlap between clusters <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e195" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e196" class="inline-graphic"></span> results in uncertain assignments of some variants, causing them to have appreciable <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e197" class="inline-graphic"></span> <em>and</em> <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e198" class="inline-graphic"></span>. This in reflected in a large relative (to the “size”, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e199" class="inline-graphic"></span>, of cluster <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e200" class="inline-graphic"></span>) cluster overlap<a name="pcbi.1003665.e201" id="pcbi.1003665.e201" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e201" class="inline-graphic"></span></p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p3" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p3" class="link-target"></a><p>Minimizing this quantity for all <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e202" class="inline-graphic"></span> is equivalent to maximizing the “self-overlap” of cluster <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e203" class="inline-graphic"></span> with itself,<a name="pcbi.1003665.e204" id="pcbi.1003665.e204" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e204" class="inline-graphic"></span>which satisfies, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e205" class="inline-graphic"></span>. Hence, we remove any cluster having a <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e206" class="inline-graphic"></span> less than a threshold <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e207" class="inline-graphic"></span>. Overlap between (independent) clusters will be more likely in lower dimensional problems; hence, to determine a dimensionality-dependent <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e208" class="inline-graphic"></span> we clustered simulated data sets by sampling a mixture of beta distributions in one, two, or three dimensions and having between two and five clusters. Average concordance (across data sets of a given dimensionality) between the clustered and known results (in terms of fraction of correctly assigned items) was stable for a wide range of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e209" class="inline-graphic"></span> within each dimension: <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e210" class="inline-graphic"></span> in the range of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e211" class="inline-graphic"></span> to <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e212" class="inline-graphic"></span> achieved the maximal concordance (of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e213" class="inline-graphic"></span>) in one dimension, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e214" class="inline-graphic"></span> in the range of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e215" class="inline-graphic"></span> to <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e216" class="inline-graphic"></span> achieved a concordance of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e217" class="inline-graphic"></span> in two dimensions, and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e218" class="inline-graphic"></span> in the range of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e219" class="inline-graphic"></span> to <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e220" class="inline-graphic"></span> achieved a concordance greater than or equal to <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e221" class="inline-graphic"></span> in three dimensions. Intuitively, we anticipate that the probability of clusters overlapping scales inversely with the number of dimensions. Hence, we define <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e222" class="inline-graphic"></span> for an <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e223" class="inline-graphic"></span>-dimensional problem as <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e224" class="inline-graphic"></span>, where <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e225" class="inline-graphic"></span> was selected so that <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e226" class="inline-graphic"></span> passes through the above optimal regions defined by the simulation. Namely, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e227" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e228" class="inline-graphic"></span>. Results for these settings of <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e229" class="inline-graphic"></span> across all simulated data sets are shown in <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s005">Fig. S5</a>.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p4" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p4" class="link-target"></a><p>We detect outliers using a more formal approach than our previous method <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Walter1" class="ref-tip">[14]</a>, by calculating the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e230" class="inline-graphic"></span>-value of a variant with the respect to the cluster to which it has been assigned (via a hard assignment). If the probability of the variant belonging to that cluster is less than <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e231" class="inline-graphic"></span>, the variant is removed from the analysis. The default used in this manuscript is <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e232" class="inline-graphic"></span> (which is <em>not</em> corrected for multiple testing). The <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e233" class="inline-graphic"></span>-value of a variant <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e234" class="inline-graphic"></span> is calculated with respect to the predictive posterior distribution [Eq. (8)] as<a name="pcbi.1003665.e235" id="pcbi.1003665.e235" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e235" class="inline-graphic"></span>where <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e236" class="inline-graphic"></span> is the Heaviside step function with <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e237" class="inline-graphic"></span> for <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e238" class="inline-graphic"></span> and <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e239" class="inline-graphic"></span> for <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e240" class="inline-graphic"></span>. In the case of beta mixture models, this integral is evaluated numerically by sampling from the predictive posterior distribution and then evaluating sampled variants with that distribution, which again involves numerical integration. For computational efficiency, we only calculate this integral for variants likely to be outliers, which we heuristically define as variants whose VAF <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e241" class="inline-graphic"></span> in each sample <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e242" class="inline-graphic"></span> lies outside of the narrowest interval containing <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e243" class="inline-graphic"></span> of the fluctuation in the mean of cluster <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e244" class="inline-graphic"></span>. This interval <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e245" class="inline-graphic"></span> is determined as the narrowest such interval satisfying<a name="pcbi.1003665.e246" id="pcbi.1003665.e246" class="link-target"></a><span class="equation"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e246" class="inline-graphic"></span>and involves integrating the mean, <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e247" class="inline-graphic"></span>, with respect to the posterior distribution.</p>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p5" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec5.p5" class="link-target"></a><p>Several iterations of the AML28 data set following the <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e248" class="inline-graphic"></span>-means initialization (above and <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s006">Fig. S6a</a>) are shown in Figs S6b and c, with the complete run shown in Movie S2.</p>
</div>

<div id="section6" class="section toc-section"><a id="s4f" name="s4f" class="link-target" title="Variant detection and copy number calling"></a>
<h3>Variant detection and copy number calling</h3>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec6.p1" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec6.p1" class="link-target"></a><p>Sequencing, alignment, and variant calling were performed as previously described <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Ding1" class="ref-tip">[5]</a>. Somatic copy number events were detected using copyCat (<a href="http://github.com/chrisamiller/copycat/">http://github.com/chrisamiller/copycat/</a>). Copy-number neutral LOH was detected using VarScan 2 <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Koboldt1" class="ref-tip">[38]</a> and filtered to retain regions with 95% LOH and at least 10 sites.</p>
</div>

<div id="section7" class="section toc-section"><a id="s4g" name="s4g" class="link-target" title="PyClone"></a>
<h3>PyClone</h3>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec7.p1" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec7.p1" class="link-target"></a><p>PyClone version 0.12.3 was downloaded from <a href="http://compbio.bccrc.ca/software/pyclone/">http://compbio.bccrc.ca/software/pyclone/</a>. VarScan 2-detected regions of LOH were excluded from analysis. Copy number events detected by copyCat were quantized and passed to PyClone as major_cn, with minor_cn set to zero; additionally, PyClone was run with ––var_prior total_copy_number, since allele-specific copy number calls were not provided. PyClone clustering used the beta-binomial mixture model. Initially, we attempted to cluster using 10,000 iterations and 1,000 burn-in iterations, as suggested by the authors (Ref. 30 and <a href="https://bitbucket.org/aroth85/pyclone/wiki/Tutorial">https://bitbucket.org/aroth85/pyclone/wiki/Tutorial</a>). However, these parameters yielded discordant clusterings across three runs. Therefore, we varied the number of total iterations (and additionally varied the number of burn-in iterations to be 10% of the total iterations) and for each configuration assessed concordance across three independent runs. The authors have suggested similar approaches based on visual inspection of convergence across randomly-initialized runs <a href="#pcbi.1003665-Roth1" class="ref-tip">[30]</a>. We choose the number of iterations at which the concordance across the three runs stabilized. These are given in <a href="#pcbi.1003665.s009">Table S1</a>. Concordance was evaluated for each of the three pairs and was calculated as the maximal fraction of items assigned to the same cluster across permutations of the cluster labels of one of the two runs being compared.</p>
</div>

<div id="section8" class="section toc-section"><a id="s4h" name="s4h" class="link-target" title="THetA"></a>
<h3>THetA</h3>
<a id="article1.body1.sec4.sec8.p1" name="article1.body1.sec4.sec8.p1" class="link-target"></a><p>THetA version 0.51 was downloaded from <a href="http://compbio.cs.brown.edu/projects/theta/">http://compbio.cs.brown.edu/projects/theta/</a>. After failing to successfully run the program on the complete set of copy number events in the MM sample, we selected seven copy number regions, representing neutral, amplified, and subclonally deleted chromosomes, and ran THetA as described in the manual (parameters: –n 3 –k 4 –m 0.10 ––NUM_PROCESSES 2). The resulting population frequencies and copy number assignments were used to infer the VAF at which a SNV in that region would appear. These sites were added to the list of SNV inputs to SciClone and clustered with default parameters.</p>
</div>
</div>

CN-derived points are highlighted in yellow. The leftmost two CN events are single points and the rightmost point consists of six overlapping points.</p>

Beta mixture modeling (<a href="#pcbi-1003665-g003">Fig. 3</a>) differs from Gaussian mixture modeling in the single variant highlighted by arrow in (a) and from binomial mixture modeling in the separation of cluster two from cluster one in (b).</p>
<p class="siDoi"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s002">https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s002</a></p><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material2.caption1.p2" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material2.caption1.p2" class="link-target"></a><p class="postSiDOI">(TIF)</p>
</div><div class="supplementary-material"><a name="pcbi.1003665.s003" id="pcbi.1003665.s003" class="link-target"></a><h3 class="siTitle title-small"><a href="article/file?type=supplementary&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s003">Figure S3. </a></h3><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material3.caption1.p1" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material3.caption1.p1" class="link-target"></a><p class="preSiDOI"><strong>Confirming subclonal AML populations using an independent method.</strong> PyClone largely recapitulates subclonal architecture inferred by SciClone (<a href="#pcbi-1003665-g003">Fig. 3</a>), though the parameter settings used here (default hyperparameters to beta-binomial mixture, with 10,000 iterations, and a burn-in of 1,000 iterations) overdissect the founding clone.</p>
<p class="siDoi"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s003">https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s003</a></p><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material3.caption1.p2" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material3.caption1.p2" class="link-target"></a><p class="postSiDOI">(TIF)</p>
</div><div class="supplementary-material"><a name="pcbi.1003665.s004" id="pcbi.1003665.s004" class="link-target"></a><h3 class="siTitle title-small"><a href="article/file?type=supplementary&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s004">Figure S4. </a></h3><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material4.caption1.p1" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material4.caption1.p1" class="link-target"></a><p class="preSiDOI"><strong>Confirming subclonal breast tumor populations using an independent method.</strong> PyClone clustering of variants in copy-number neutral regions is similar to that obtained by SciClone (<a href="#pcbi-1003665-g005">Fig. 5</a>), though the former partitions the variants spread along the pre-treatment tumor 2 axis (clusters 1 and 2), as well as those belonging to the founding clone (clusters 7 and 9). Subpanels (a–c) correspond to two-dimensional slices in <a href="#pcbi-1003665-g005">Fig. 5</a> of three breast tumor samples (two spatially distinct samples from a primary tumor and one sample taken after aromatase-inhibitor treatment).</p>
<p class="siDoi"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s004">https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s004</a></p><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material4.caption1.p2" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material4.caption1.p2" class="link-target"></a><p class="postSiDOI">(TIF)</p>
</div><div class="supplementary-material"><a name="pcbi.1003665.s005" id="pcbi.1003665.s005" class="link-target"></a><h3 class="siTitle title-small"><a href="article/file?type=supplementary&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s005">Figure S5. </a></h3><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material5.caption1.p1" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material5.caption1.p1" class="link-target"></a><p class="preSiDOI"><strong>Assessing concordance between known and clustered results.</strong> Beta mixtures having two to six components were sampled in (a) one, (b) two, or (c) dimensions and clustered. Concordance is the fraction of data points correctly clustered; the highest concordance resulting from a permutation of the cluster labels is reported. Reported self-overlap is the minimum reported over any cluster, i.e., <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e249" class="inline-graphic"></span>. Self-overlap is shifted by 0.1 in the plots for visual purposes to avoid obscuring concordance.</p>
<p class="siDoi"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s005">https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s005</a></p><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material5.caption1.p2" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material5.caption1.p2" class="link-target"></a><p class="postSiDOI">(TIF)</p>
</div><div class="supplementary-material"><a name="pcbi.1003665.s006" id="pcbi.1003665.s006" class="link-target"></a><h3 class="siTitle title-small"><a href="article/file?type=supplementary&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s006">Figure S6. </a></h3><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material6.caption1.p1" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material6.caption1.p1" class="link-target"></a><p class="preSiDOI"><strong>Converging to clustering solution using variational Bayesian beta mixture model.</strong> <span class="inline-formula"><img src="article/file?type=thumbnail&amp;id=info:doi/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.e250" class="inline-graphic"></span>-means initialization (A) of AML sample (<a href="#pcbi-1003665-g003">Fig. 3</a>) and results following second (B) and fourth steps (of six) in iteration (C).</p>
<p class="siDoi"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s006">https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003665.s006</a></p><a id="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material6.caption1.p2" name="article1.body1.sec5.supplementary-material6.caption1.p2" class="link-target"></a><p class="postSiDOI">(TIF)</p>
